# ROADMAP
## Product Launch Operating System (PLOS) — Development Execution Plan

**Last updated:** May 15, 2026 (**W#2 P-12 SHIPPED at code level on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` — extension 401-retry / silent-refresh analog to P-1.** Eightieth Claude Code session. Director's launch prompt named (a.14) explicitly; this session executed it. `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/api-client.ts` `authedFetch` refactored to a factory `makeAuthedFetch({ supabase, fetchFn })` mirroring P-1's `makeAuthFetch` in `src/lib/authFetch.ts`. On 401, the wrapper calls `supabase.auth.refreshSession()` once + retries with the new access token; on refresh failure, returns the original 401 unchanged so the caller's existing `PlosApiError(401)` error path is preserved. Production export wraps `fetch` in an arrow `(u, i) => fetch(u, i)` to preserve the window receiver — applying the P-17 lesson from the 2026-05-12 hotfix `08f10e5`. Pre-fetch no-token check still throws `PlosApiError(401, "Not signed in")`; `mapFetchTransportError` wrapping applied to BOTH the first attempt and the retry (TypeError → `PlosApiError(0, "Network unreachable")` semantics survive across the silent-refresh path). **Tests added:** `api-client.test.ts` extended with 9 new tests mirroring `src/lib/authFetch.test.ts`'s 7-test pattern plus 2 extension-specific cases (TypeError on first attempt; TypeError on retry after successful refresh). Test count 252 → 261. **Verification scoreboard:** 261/261 ext tests pass; `tsc --noEmit` clean; `wxt build` clean (6 artifacts at 676K — baseline parity). **Branch state at session start:** W#2 was 4 commits behind `origin/main` (P-17 + Rule 27 + platform-UI fix-pair + 2026-05-12-b deploy doc-batch); director picked merge over rebase via Rule 14f forced-picker; `git merge origin/main` FAST-FORWARDED cleanly (zero conflicts) because main's 2026-05-12-b deploy session had already absorbed W#2's prior 2026-05-12 doc-batch commit `23375bd`. **Previously updated:** May 12, 2026 (**W#2 verification session + vklf.com production hotfix.** Seventy-sixth Claude Code session. Launch-prompt task was the deferred verification queue (P3B-1..P3B-11 cross-device sign-in test deferred twice; P1V-1..P1V-3 silent token refresh tests; S4-A + S4-B + S4-C Module 2 text-capture walkthroughs). **HIGH-severity production hotfix shipped to main mid-session:** `src/lib/authFetch.ts:82` had a bare-`fetch` reference (`fetchFn: fetch`) introduced 2026-05-10-f with the P-1 silent token refresh; browsers detach `fetch` when invoked via a detached reference and throw `TypeError: Failed to execute 'fetch' on 'Window': Illegal invocation`. The bug broke every authenticated page load on vklf.com but was invisible during deploy sessions #4 + #5 because both ended within the 1-hour access-token freshness window (the silent refresh path that surfaces the bug was never exercised). Director hit the bug at S4-A-4 today. tsc clean; build clean (51 routes — baseline parity); Vercel auto-redeploy `state: success` per `gh api deployments/4650327672/statuses`; director verified vklf.com loads cleanly post-deploy. **Test-coverage gap captured as P-17** — all 7 P-1 unit tests inject a fake `fetchFn`; doc-drift on "red error" wording captured); P3B-1..P3B-10 PASS (canonical cross-device proof on laptop 2 with fresh-install chrome.storage.local); P3B-11 N/A. **Six DEFERRED polish items captured this session per Rule 14e + Rule 26 — destinations all in W#2 polish backlog this same doc-batch:** P-12 extension 401-retry / silent-refresh analog to P-1; surfaced only via S4-B's selection gesture); P-15 `pickInitialUrl` missing `canonicalProductUrl` step on slug-variant URLs (session-4 bug — overlay fails to pre-select current page's URL when path has Amazon-style product slug); ## NEW W#2 polish items added 2026-05-12 (P-12 through P-17)

Six polish items captured during today's verification session + hotfix. Full root-cause + fix details in `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_DESIGN.md` §B 2026-05-12 entry and in `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Outcome 2026-05-12 block. Brief listing here for the polish-backlog index:

- **P-12** Extension 401-retry / silent-refresh analog to P-1. **Where:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/api-client.ts authedFetch`. **Status:** ✅ SHIPPED at code level 2026-05-15 on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` (commit `414efe6` — refactor to factory `makeAuthedFetch({ supabase, fetchFn })` + 9 new unit tests; 261/261 ext tests pass; deploy pending per (a.15) above). **Severity:** MEDIUM. **Why:** Extension popup's API client had no 401-retry until this session; transient 401s surfaced as "broken popup" state until the popup was re-opened. P-1 shipped this pattern for vklf.com web (`src/lib/authFetch.ts`) on 2026-05-10-f; the extension's API path now has the same wrapper. **Fix shipped:** factory `makeAuthedFetch({ supabase, fetchFn })` returns the actual `authedFetch`; on 401, calls `supabase.auth.refreshSession()` once and retries with the new token; if refresh fails, returns original 401 unchanged. Production export wraps `fetch` in arrow per P-17 lesson.

- **P-13** Autofocus on "+ Add new…" inline category input (popup + overlay). **Where:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/entrypoints/popup/components/CapturedTextPasteForm.tsx` AND `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/text-capture-form.ts`. **Status:** OPEN. **Severity:** LOW. **Why:** Director-requested at S4-A-5 — when user picks "+ Add new…" from category dropdown, the inline name-input that appears should auto-receive focus so user can immediately start typing. Currently requires an extra click. **Fix shape:** ~2 lines per file — `inputRef.current?.focus()` via useEffect on mount OR `autoFocus` prop on the inline input element.

- **P-14** Highlight-terms applicator + MutationObserver self-feedback loop causes flashing on all platforms. **Where:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/orchestrator.ts` MutationObserver setup ~line 297 + `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/highlight-terms.ts refresh()`. **Status:** OPEN. **Severity:** MEDIUM-HIGH. **PRE-EXISTING since 2026-05-08-d P-5 ship** — only became visible-as-blocker today because S4-B's selection gesture surfaces it. **Why:** Orchestrator's MO observes `document.body` with `childList: true, subtree: true` on every mutation; debounced callback (RESCAN_DEBOUNCE_MS=250) calls `highlighter.refresh()` which strips all `<mark>` elements then re-applies them — both DOM mutations trigger MO again. Self-feedback loop. Host-page activity (lazy-loaded images, ads, hover effects) feeds the loop independently. Visible flashing at ~250ms cadence; selection on highlighted text destroyed every cycle. **Fix shape:** disconnect+reconnect MO around each refresh pass OR filter mutations whose target is a `<mark>` element OR set a "we're mutating" flag the MO callback short-circuits on. Must regression-test P-10 SPA navigation detection still works.

- **P-15** `pickInitialUrl` missing `platformModule.canonicalProductUrl(...)` step on slug-variant URLs. **Where:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/text-capture-form.ts:459` call site (the `captured-text-validation.ts pickInitialUrl` function itself is correct in isolation; the bug is the caller skipping canonicalization). **Status:** OPEN. **Severity:** MEDIUM (user-visible UX miss; workaround is one extra dropdown click). **Session-4 bug.** **Why:** When user right-clicks on a saved competitor page, overlay form's URL picker fails to auto-pre-select that page's saved URL because Amazon/etc. serve the same product under multiple paths (with and without product-name slug). The "already saved" banner path in `orchestrator.ts:251-256` first passes location.href through `platformModule.canonicalProductUrl(...)` BEFORE normalizing; the pre-fill path skips that step. **Fix shape:** in `text-capture-form.ts:459`, canonicalize before passing to pickInitialUrl: `pickInitialUrl(platformModule.canonicalProductUrl(props.pageUrl) ?? props.pageUrl, rows)`. Add a regression-test case to `captured-text-validation.test.ts` using a fake `platformModule.canonicalProductUrl`.

- **P-16** Extension service worker "went to a bad state unexpectedly" — surfaced on laptop 2 during P3B walkthrough. **Where:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/entrypoints/background.ts`. **Status:** OPEN. **Severity:** MEDIUM. **Why:** Chrome's chrome://extensions on laptop 2 showed the extension's MV3 service worker had crashed at some point ("Service worker went to a bad state unexpectedly. Context is unknown. Stack Trace: :0 (anonymous function)"). Degenerate stack trace — Chrome doesn't have meaningful source info, suggesting the crash came from an async path the source map doesn't cover. Chrome auto-restarts the SW on next event, so user-visible impact is intermittent (popup + context-menu remain functional after restart). **Diagnosis steps:** click "Inspect views: service worker" on the extension card → SW's own DevTools shows the real stack. Likely causes: (1) Supabase auto-refresh-token loop fired during P3B-9's WiFi-off period and threw an unhandled promise rejection (MV3 SWs are stricter than persistent backgrounds); (2) chrome.runtime.onMessage handlers hit an unhandled error in one of the session-4 async paths (`createCapturedText`, `listVocabularyEntries`, `createVocabularyEntry`). **Fix shape:** wrap onMessage handler's async paths in try/catch with structured sendResponse on error; ensure Supabase auto-refresh failures are caught (Supabase swallows refresh errors internally, but the MV3 SW may surface them via a different path).

- **P-17** Real-fetch integration test for `authFetch.ts` production export. **Where:** `src/lib/authFetch.ts` production export (line 81-88) + new `tests/playwright/` harness. **Status:** ✅ SHIPPED at code level 2026-05-14 (Seventy-ninth Claude Code session, on `main`). **Severity:** MEDIUM (process polish, not user-facing). **Why:** Test-coverage gap that allowed the 2026-05-12 `Illegal invocation` regression to ship. All 7 existing unit tests in `authFetch.test.ts` inject a fake `fetchFn` via `makeAuthFetch({ fetchFn: <fake> })`; none exercise the production export's `fetchFn: fetch` bare-reference wiring (which is the line that had the bug). Node's fetch is more lenient than browser fetch, so even an integration test in node wouldn't catch this. **Fix shape (locked at session start via Rule 14f forced-picker; director picked Option A):** Playwright suite in real Chromium. Catches the regression CLASS, not just the exact 2026-05-12 bug shape, because the real Chromium engine enforces the receiver-binding rule at the C++ level. **What was actually shipped:** `tests/playwright/authFetch-regression.spec.ts` with 2 tests (200 path + 401-refresh-retry path), both asserting `threwIllegalInvocation: false`. Supporting infra: tiny stub HTTP server, esbuild-bundled `src/lib/authFetch.ts` with `@supabase/supabase-js` aliased to a local fake (so the production-export wiring runs end-to-end without a real Supabase), Playwright config, npm scripts `test:e2e` + `test:e2e:install`. Sanity-checked in-session: reverting line 84-88 to bare `fetch` makes both Playwright tests fail LOUDLY with the expected error. Cross-references: commit `08f10e5` (the original hotfix); CORRECTIONS_LOG 2026-05-12 entry (the Lessons block); README §"Running the Playwright regression tests" (system-libs install workaround for fresh Codespaces).

- **P-18** Devcontainer postCreateCommand for Chromium system libraries. **Where:** new `.devcontainer/devcontainer.json` (or equivalent Codespace config). **Status:** OPEN. **Severity:** LOW (developer ergonomics only — Playwright tests have a documented manual workaround that resolves in ~2 minutes). **Why:** P-17's Playwright suite requires GTK/X11 system libs (libatk, libxfixes, libgbm, libnss3, libnspr4 etc.) that the default Codespaces Ubuntu 24.04 image doesn't ship. Codespaces system-package state does NOT persist across rebuilds, so every fresh Codespace hits `error while loading shared libraries: libatk-1.0.so.0` on first `npm run test:e2e`. Playwright's recommended `npx playwright install --with-deps chromium` doesn't work here because the Codespace's `/etc/apt/sources.list.d/yarn.list` has an unverifiable GPG signature that blocks `apt update`. **Fix shape:** add a `.devcontainer/devcontainer.json` with `postCreateCommand` (or `onCreateCommand`) that runs the manual workaround from `README.md` §"Running the Playwright regression tests" — temporarily disable yarn.list, install the lib set, restore yarn.list. **Pre-capture search per Rule 24:** searched docs (none), repo root (no `.devcontainer/` directory exists today). Cross-cutting platform-side polish (not strictly W#2) — captured under W#2 polish backlog for now alongside P-17 follow-on; future session can re-categorize as platform-wide if needed. Cross-references: CORRECTIONS_LOG 2026-05-14 INFORMATIONAL entry (full diagnosis); README §"Running the Playwright regression tests".

**Previously updated:** May 10, 2026-b (**W#2 polish session #8 — P-2 + P-9 + P-10 polish bundle SHIPPED at code level on `workflow-2-competition-scraping`.** Three extension-only fixes in one bundle. **(P-2) `authedFetch` offline error handling** — wrapped `fetch()` in try/catch; new exported `mapFetchTransportError(err)` helper converts native `TypeError("Failed to fetch")` (offline / DNS failure / CORS preflight failure / refused connection) → `PlosApiError(0, 'Network unreachable — check your connection.')`; AbortError + other shapes re-thrown unchanged; new test file `api-client.test.ts` with 6 tests covering all the conversion cases. **(P-10) AlreadySavedOverlay reliability on Walmart heavy-SPA pages** — three orchestrator changes: (1) `maybeShowDetailOverlay()` dedupes by `location.href` via new `lastOverlayUrl` closure variable (set BEFORE recognition match so navigate-away-and-back correctly re-fires); (2) new `scheduleDetailOverlayCheck()` 150ms-debounced cancellable timer ensures only the final URL gets a banner check after pushState bursts; (3) MutationObserver-based SPA URL change detection via new `lastObservedUrl` closure variable — checks `location.href !== lastObservedUrl` inside the existing 250ms-debounced rescan callback and triggers the overlay-check debouncer if changed. **Critical technical wrinkle that drove the design:** Chrome content scripts run in an **isolated world** with their own `window.history`, so patching `pushState` in content-script context does NOT intercept host-page React Router calls (Walmart, etc.) — the MutationObserver is the cross-context-safe signal since SPA navigation always causes immediate DOM mutation. **(P-9) Live-page Highlight Terms 500KB body-text cap REMOVED entirely** — replaced with chunked/incremental highlight pass via `requestIdleCallback`. New exported `processInChunks<T>(items, processItem, options)` generic helper (default chunk size 500 nodes ≈ 10-15ms/chunk; pluggable `yieldFn` for testing; honors `CancellationSignal` between chunks). `applyHighlightsTo` is now async + chunked; `startLiveHighlighting.refresh()` rewritten for last-wins cancellation (each new refresh cancels in-flight pass before starting; latest DOM/term state always becomes eventual visible state). Removing the cap auto-resolves the backlog's recommended (e) dedupe warning + (f) skip-if-unchanged measurement — no cap → no warning to dedupe → no `document.body.textContent.length` re-measure overhead. 9 new tests added to `highlight-terms.test.ts` for `processInChunks` (chunk boundaries, ordering invariant, cancellation mid-pass, cancellation before first item, default chunkSize). **Verification scoreboard:** ext compile clean; Three real bugs in extension session 3 code surfaced + FIXED INLINE in single code commit `f4226ca`: (1) **content-script CORS blocker** (the original attempt #3 trigger) — content scripts run in host page's origin (amazon.com etc.) which is NOT in vklf.com's CORS allowlist (`chrome-extension://*` only), so `listCompetitorUrls` + `createCompetitorUrl` direct fetches failed preflight with `TypeError: Failed to fetch`. (a.13) 🛡️ P-17 real-fetch integration test for `authFetch.ts` production export — RECOMMENDED-NEXT on `main`. Captured 2026-05-12 from the vklf.com `Illegal invocation` hotfix root-cause analysis: the production export at `src/lib/authFetch.ts:82` passed `fetch` bare as `fetchFn`, which browsers detach from the window receiver and reject with `TypeError: Failed to execute 'fetch' on 'Window': Illegal invocation`. All 7 existing unit tests inject a fake `fetchFn` via the DI seam — the production wiring line itself was never exercised. Node's fetch is more lenient than browser fetch, so a node-context integration test wouldn't catch it either; need a jsdom or Playwright browser-context test. Scope: ~30–60 LOC test that imports the production export, exercises a real (mocked but realistic) authenticated fetch through the production wiring, asserts no `Illegal invocation` thrown. Cross-references: `src/lib/authFetch.ts:81-88` (the fixed production export); `src/lib/authFetch.test.ts` (the 7-test suite that doesn't cover production wiring); commit `08f10e5` (the 2026-05-12 hotfix). **Branch:** `main` (platform infrastructure used by W#1 + W#2 + future workflows). **Pre-session terminal commands:** `cd /workspaces/brand-operations-hub && git fetch origin && git checkout main && git pull --rebase origin main`. **Launch prompt** *(paste as first message in fresh Claude Code session)*: *"Read docs/CLAUDE_CODE_STARTER.md and follow every rule in it. **Status-cell vocabulary:** 🆕 about-to-start / 🔄 active-dev / 🛠 schema-change-session / ✅ graduated / ⏸ paused / — no-current-work. See `MULTI_WORKFLOW_PROTOCOL.md` §5 for definitions.

## The 4-phase model (canonical)

Per `PLATFORM_REQUIREMENTS.md §11`, platform development is structured around four phases. This roadmap restructures all roadmap items into these phases.

```
Phase 1 — Admin-solo tooling
  Goal: admin runs 50 Projects/week solo through all 14 workflows
  Gate to Phase 2: all 14 workflow tools built; one end-to-end Project completed

Phase 2 — Multi-user infrastructure
  Goal: platform ready for worker onboarding
  Gate to Phase 3: infrastructure complete; 1 test worker running successfully

Phase 3 — Worker ramp
  Goal: scale from 1 test worker to 50 workers at 500 Projects/week
  Gate to Phase 4: stable 500/week operation

Phase 4 — Scale hardening
  Goal: scale from 500/week to 5,000/week
  Gate: ongoing
```

---

## 🚨 HIGH (2026-05-04-c; updated 2026-05-04-d) — Pool exhaustion under apply-pipeline burst (`FATAL: Max client connections reached`) — fires ON PRO TIER; pool tune INSUFFICIENT; code-fix required

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-04-c. **POOL-TUNE TRIED 2026-05-04-d — INSUFFICIENT.** Director bumped pool size from default 15 to 40 (67% of Nano compute's Postgres max_connections=60 cap; comfortably below Supabase's 80% instability warning). Small-batch test on Bursitis Test 2 batch 2 produced same failure. Pool tune at this compute tier is structurally insufficient; **code-fix is now PRIMARY and gate-blocking** (see "Fix layers" below). Pool size 40 stays in place as secondary buffer.

**🚨 BURST-SIZE CORRECTION 2026-05-04-d:** the 2026-05-04-c estimate of "~22 parallel PATCH /keywords/[id] calls per batch" was WRONG by a factor of ~2.5×. Vercel log expansion in tonight's session revealed **the actual burst is 55-60+ parallel PATCH calls per batch** (counted: ~40 successful PATCH 200s + ~18 PATCH 500s in a 3-second window during Bursitis Test 2 batch 2 with 19 operations applied). The 2026-05-04-c estimate was based on a Vercel view that showed only failures (collapsed/filtered); tonight's expanded view shows the full burst. All prior reasoning that assumed "22-burst" needs recalibration: at 50-Phase-3-workers × 60-burst = **3,000 simultaneous connections at peak** — uncoverable by any compute tier upgrade Supabase offers (largest tier 16XL caps at ~12,000 max client + ~128 default pool size; even with 3000 connections of headroom, the per-pool default would need radical custom tuning).

**The problem:** the apply-pipeline fires **~55-60+ parallel PATCH /keywords/[id]** requests per batch (one per touched keyword) when applying batch results to the canvas. (Was estimated ~22 in 2026-05-04-c entry; corrected 2026-05-04-d after Vercel log expansion.) Each parallel request opens a Prisma connection through Supabase's pgbouncer transaction pooler at port 6543. Supabase Free-tier pool capacity is overwhelmed. Postgres returns `FATAL: Max client connections reached` to every request beyond the limit. The error surfaces as `PrismaClientUnknownRequestError` or `PrismaClientInitializationError` with NO Prisma error code — just the FATAL message embedded in `error.message`. Cascade: ~28 cascading 500s within ~0.1 sec at 8:30:40 PM in the 2026-05-04-c D3 batch 1 (~22 PATCH /keywords/[id] failures + 4 GET /canvas + 2 GET /canvas/nodes failures).

**Why the 2026-05-04-b withRetry rate-fix doesn't help:** withRetry retries Prisma codes P1001/P1002/P1008/P2034. Pool exhaustion has no Prisma code. Even if it WERE matched as transient, retrying immediately worsens pool pressure (each retry attempts another connection while the pool is full). **Retries cannot fix capacity.**

**Fix layers (in order — REVISED 2026-05-04-d after empirical pool-tune test):**

1. ✅ **Supabase Pro upgrade — DONE 2026-05-04-b.** Pro plan unlocks the configurable pool-size knob (Free hides it); but Pro plan default compute is **Nano** (smallest available) — the upgrade did NOT auto-bump compute. Underlying Postgres `max_connections` stays at 60 on Nano regardless of plan tier.

1a. 🟡 **Pool size config knob tuning — TRIED 2026-05-04-d, INSUFFICIENT.** Director bumped pool size from default 15 → 40 (67% of Nano compute's 60-cap; comfortably below Supabase's 80% warning threshold which fires at 48). Small-batch test outcome: pool 40 absorbed ~40 of the 55-60+ burst; ~18+ still failed with FATAL. Pool 48 (max safe under warning) would be ~10 short of the burst peak. Pool 60 (100% of max_connections) hits Supabase's instability warning. **No safe pool size at Nano compute absorbs the actual burst.** The pool size 40 stays in place as a secondary buffer (still helping); the structural answer is layer (2) below.

2. ❌ **Apply-pipeline parallel-PATCH-burst reduction — NOW PRIMARY (gate-blocking 2026-05-04-d).** Three approaches (revised with corrected burst size):
   - **(i) Worker queue (client-side throttle).** Serialize the 55-60+ parallel PATCHes via a small worker queue (e.g., 10 simultaneous max). ~10-20 LOC change in `AutoAnalyze.tsx`. **Quality impact: ZERO** (same operations, same final canvas state — just sequenced over slightly more wall-clock time). Speed impact: each batch's apply phase ~3-6 seconds longer (negligible vs. ~90-second model phase). Risk: lowest. Doesn't fix the P2025 race condition (see separate entry).
   - **(ii) Bulk PATCH /keywords endpoint.** Use the existing `PATCH /keywords` endpoint that accepts arrays. Send all 55-60 updates in one HTTP request instead of separate ones. **Quality impact: ZERO** if the bulk endpoint covers all needed fields (audit needed; may need small extensions). Speed impact: faster (fewer round trips). Risk: medium. May or may not fix P2025 race depending on internal sequencing.
   - **(iii) Atomic batch into canvas-rebuild $transaction.** Fold the keyword updates into the same `$transaction` that already rebuilds the canvas. One transaction; all updates atomic. **Quality impact: ZERO. Reliability impact: IMPROVES — eliminates the P2025 race for free.** Speed impact: potentially faster (one transaction vs. many round trips). Risk: highest — larger refactor; need to keep transaction within timeout bounds. **Most thorough and reliable per director's standing preference; likely recommendation pending code review.**

   Director chooses approach at next session's start after Claude reads `src/lib/operation-applier.ts` + `src/app/projects/[projectId]/keyword-clustering/components/AutoAnalyze.tsx` + the canvas-rebuild route. Effort: 1-2 sessions design + first-pass implementation.

3. **Pre-flight pool-config visibility check (LOW priority addition).** Pre-flight runner could surface the active Supabase compute tier + configured pool size at run start, with a warning if the pool size looks too small for the expected batch's parallel-PATCH count. Nice-to-have once layer (2) ships. ~10-20 LOC.

4. **Compute tier upgrade (LOW priority — symptom treatment, not root cause).** Going Nano → Micro/Small adds CPU/RAM but max_connections stays at 200 on those tiers. Medium ($60/mo) gets max_connections=400; Large ($110/mo) gets 600; XL ($210/mo) gets 700; 2XL ($410/mo) gets 1500. Even 2XL's 1500 won't comfortably absorb Phase 3's 50 × 60 = 3000 burst. **Compute upgrade is treating-the-symptom money; layer (2) is the structural answer.** Could be considered as a Phase 2 bridge if Phase 2 multi-user transition starts before layer (2) ships, but not before then.

**Phase 3 implication (zoom-out per Rule 16):** at 50 concurrent workers (Phase 3 scale target per `PLATFORM_REQUIREMENTS.md §1`), pool exhaustion will be vastly worse than today's solo-director load. Pro upgrade is necessary but not sufficient — the apply-pipeline parallel-burst pattern itself needs revisiting before Phase 3, OR the connection pool needs further tuning beyond Pro's defaults. Architectural concern that propagates to W#2-W#14 because they share the same DB + pool.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-04-C-D3-RETRY-PARTIAL-POOL-EXHAUSTION-FINDING STATE block (full forensic detail); `PLATFORM_ARCHITECTURE.md §10` "🚨 Connection pool exhaustion under apply-pipeline burst" entry (platform-level technical debt registry); `CORRECTIONS_LOG.md` 2026-05-04-c INFORMATIONAL entry (process lesson on rate-fix scope vs. discovered failure mode).

## 🔍 NEW MEDIUM (2026-05-04-d) — P2025 race condition between canvas-rebuild's archive and parallel keyword PATCHes

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-04-d during pool-tune small-batch test Vercel log analysis.

**The finding:** during Bursitis Test 2 batch 2's apply pipeline at 23:08:06 UTC, the canvas-rebuild `$transaction` archived 2 keywords (Greg Hayes proper-name + Capsella bursa-pastoris botanical Latin — both correct semantic calls). In the same window, the parallel PATCH /keywords/[id] burst was firing. One of the failed PATCHes (keyword `78c696c5`) returned a **DIFFERENT error type** than the rest of the burst: `P2025 "No record was found for an update"` — a Prisma "record doesn't exist" error, NOT pool exhaustion (which has no Prisma code).

**Most likely cause:** race condition where the rebuild archived/relocated the keyword while a parallel PATCH was still in-flight against it. The PATCH read the keyword state pre-archive, computed an update, fired the update — and by the time the update reached Postgres, the keyword had been moved/archived by the rebuild transaction.

**Why MEDIUM, not HIGH:** isolated occurrence (1 of 58 PATCHes); the operation that "lost" was a placement update on an archived keyword, which is by definition a no-op once archived. No data corruption; no quality impact. But the failure surfaces as a 500 to the user, which is bad UX.

**Fix relationship to Pool exhaustion entry:**
- Approach (i) worker queue: doesn't fix this; the race can still happen at the boundary between rebuild-transaction-finishing and the next worker-queue-batch firing.
- Approach (ii) bulk PATCH endpoint: may or may not fix this depending on whether the endpoint sequences the updates relative to the rebuild transaction.
- Approach (iii) atomic-batch-into-rebuild-transaction: **eliminates this race for free** because all updates apply atomically with the archive. Strong reason to favor (iii).

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-04-D STATE block; the "Bonus finding" section.

---

## 🔍 NEW MEDIUM (2026-05-04-d) — Pre-flight check results not visible to director on Resume click

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-04-d after director's repeated correction across multiple sessions.

**The problem:** when director clicks the Resume button in the Auto-Analyze overlay, the 12 pre-flight checks (P1-P12 per 2026-05-02 instrumentation, including the new P11+P12 for consolidation prompt validation) run somewhere — server side, browser console, or silently — but **DO NOT display visibly in the overlay UI to the director**. Director has flagged this in 2026-05-04-d session and earlier sessions. Implication: director cannot independently verify which checks passed/failed before the run fires. If a check fails silently and the run aborts, director has no visibility into why. Even worse: Claude has repeatedly mis-described the click→pre-flight visibility flow because there's no observable surface to verify Claude's claims against.

**Suggested implementation:** a small panel/modal that appears on Resume click showing P1-P12 with ✓/✗ + brief description per check; persists until first batch starts. ~50-100 LOC UI work in `AutoAnalyze.tsx`.

**Priority:** elevated within Phase-1 polish bundle because it (a) affects director's ability to self-verify a pre-run safety check and (b) eliminates a recurring slip pattern from Claude (assuming visibility that doesn't exist). Standalone session candidate or first item in next polish bundle.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-04-D STATE block standing instruction (d); `CORRECTIONS_LOG.md` 2026-05-04-d entry on recurring pre-flight visibility slip.

The "Auto-Analyze started" banner shows Model + Processing Mode + Scope but also omits Thinking Mode/Budget. Director flagged this 2026-05-05-d when prompted to verify thinking config — had to open settings panel manually because activity log didn't surface it.

## 🚨 NEW HIGH (2026-05-05-d) — Auto-Analyze action history table + per-action undo

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-05-d when director surfaced as a question: "Where is the table where I can check all the actions taken by the AI model during auto-analyze and how can I interact with those actions and undo specific actions." Investigation confirmed feature does NOT exist today.

**The gap (verified by code investigation 2026-05-05-d):**

1. **`useEmitAuditEvent()` is a Phase 2 stub** (`src/lib/workflow-components/use-workflow-context.tsx:193-206`): explicitly marked "Phase 2 stub"; implementation is a no-op:
   ```javascript
   const emitAuditEvent: (eventType: string, payload: object) => Promise<void> =
     useCallback(async () => {
       // No-op in Phase 1.
     }, []);
   ```
2. **No persistent audit table in Prisma** (`prisma/schema.prisma`): no `AuditEvent` or similar table. `RemovedKeyword` (only event-like model) is for soft-archives only, not an audit log.
3. **Activity log during runs is in-memory only** (`AutoAnalyze.tsx:77-81, 1159-1161`): `LogEntry[]` lives in component local state; cleared when overlay closes; never persisted.
4. **Undo exists only at workflow level** — destructive `<ResetWorkflowButton>` (type-the-project-name confirmation) wipes all workflow data. No per-action undo.

**In practice:** the 2026-05-05-d D3 resume run executed hundreds of AI ops across 86 batches + 8 consolidations. On-canvas results persist, but there's no "this is what happened during the 5:02 PM run" record. Director cannot retrospectively review or surgically undo any individual op (e.g., reverse a specific bulk-archive item).

**Work split (each is its own item under this parent entry):**

1. **DB schema design.** New `AuditEvent` table (eventType, payload JSON, projectWorkflowId, sessionId, batchNumber, timestamp, actionableUntil, undone bool, undoneAt, undoneBy). Consider partition strategy + retention policy.
2. **Emission wiring.** Wire `useEmitAuditEvent()` from no-op to real DB insert in every operation-applier path (`operation-applier.ts`). Confirm coverage across all op types (CREATE_TOPIC, MERGE_TOPICS, MOVE_KEYWORD, ARCHIVE_KEYWORD, ADD/REMOVE_SISTER_LINK, etc.).
3. **UI surface.** New "Action History" tab in AST panel — scrollable list of all ops, filters by run / batch / op type, expand-row for full op detail.
4. **Per-action undo (DESIGN BEFORE BUILD).** Some ops are easy reverses (ADD_SISTER_LINK ↔ REMOVE_SISTER_LINK); others compose nontrivially (CREATE_TOPIC + N MOVE_KEYWORD ops to it; ARCHIVE_KEYWORD + downstream consolidation effects). Need design session before implementing — surface to director then.

**Effort estimate:** 3-5 sessions total. Could parallelize with W#1 graduation since this work is largely additive.

**Why HIGH priority:** without action history + undo, users have no surgical recovery path from over-aggressive AI decisions. The D3 run's bulk-archive consolidation #8 (117 archives) is a concrete example where review-after-the-fact would be valuable. Currently the only recovery is full workflow reset.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-05-D STATE block; `WORKFLOW_COMPONENTS_LIBRARY_DESIGN.md` (Phase 2 stub mention of `useEmitAuditEvent()`).

## 🔍 NEW MEDIUM (2026-05-05-d) — Auto-Analyze cost forecasting + credit-balance check (consolidates two findings)

**Status:** Two findings from 2026-05-05-d D3 resume session consolidate into one feature:

**Finding A — Anthropic API credit exhaustion mid-run (NEW operational risk).** Batch 85 failed all 3 retries at 8:06:52 PM with `HTTP 400: Your credit balance is too low to access the Anthropic API. Please go to Plans & Billing to upgrade or purchase credits.` Run halted ~36 min until director topped up credits at ~8:42:28 PM. Batch 85 attempt 4 succeeded post-resume. **No proactive warning** before failure; pre-flight runner does NOT check credit balance vs. estimated run cost.

**Finding B — Cost forecasting feature director request.** Auto-Analyze overlay shows running cumulative cost but no estimated remaining or estimated total. Director requested both surfaces.

**Proposed combined implementation:**

**Sliding-window cost estimator algorithm:**
- `avg_batch_cost` = average of last 10 successful batches' costs (sliding window — auto-adapts as canvas grows; falls back to first-3 average until 10 batches have run)
- `batches_remaining` = `total_batches - completed_batches`
- `avg_cons_cost` = sliding average of all consolidations so far, or $0.55 fallback until 2+ cons have fired
- `cons_remaining` = `floor(batches_remaining / cons_cadence)` (default cadence 10)
- `estimated_remaining_cost` = `(avg_batch × batches_remaining) + (avg_cons × cons_remaining)`
- `estimated_total_cost` = `current_cumulative + estimated_remaining`

**Display in Auto-Analyze overlay header (updates after each batch):**
*"Spent: $X.XX | Est. remaining: $Y.YY | Est. total: $Z.ZZ"*

**Credit-balance integration:**
- Query Anthropic balance at run start + every 10 batches via the appropriate Anthropic SDK endpoint
- Display "Available credits: $A.AA" alongside the cost estimates
- Warn yellow if `estimated_remaining > available × 0.5`
- Warn red if `estimated_remaining > available × 0.8`
- Abort with clear message if `estimated_remaining > available` (don't launch a run that can't complete)

**Why sliding-window matters:** D3 resume's per-batch cost grew $0.46 → $0.63 (early → late) due to canvas growth (195 → 242 topics). Fixed-average estimator would have under-projected by ~30% by run end. Sliding window auto-adapts.

**Effort:** ~50-100 LOC in `AutoAnalyze.tsx` + small Anthropic balance query helper. Probable single-session build.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-05-D STATE block "🚨 New findings surfaced this session" #1 and #2; `INPUT_CONTEXT_SCALING_DESIGN.md` §6 D3 RESUME COMPLETED outcome (cost trajectory data).

---

## 🔍 NEW MEDIUM (2026-05-05-d) — Late-run validation-retry rate telemetry

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-05-d during D3 RESUME COMPLETED 86-batch run.

**The finding:** earlier batches (1-30) missed at most 1 keyword on first validation attempt and recovered on retry. Late batches at canvas ≥235 (specifically batches 78 and 80) missed 5 keywords each on first attempt; cost doubled twice ($1.316 + $1.187). Retry recovered cleanly both times.

**Hypothesis:** at >150k input tokens with a large TSV input, the model occasionally drops keywords from the output payload. Earlier batches had smaller inputs and consistent 1-or-fewer-miss validation behavior; the 5-miss pattern at canvas ≥235 may indicate an emergent behavior that wasn't visible at smaller scale.

**Recommended fix posture:** **instrument first, decide if behavioral fix is needed later.** Add a mid-run dashboard metric "validation retry rate per 10 batches" (sliding window). If it crosses 30% in any 10-batch window, surface as a yellow warning in the activity log. Don't try to fix the underlying model behavior yet — measure first across multiple D3-class runs to see if it generalizes or was specific to this canvas/run shape.

**Effort:** ~30-50 LOC instrumentation. Behavioral fix (if needed later) would be its own session — possibly batch-size adjustment at large canvas, or input-shape audit.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-05-D STATE block "🚨 New findings surfaced this session" #3.

---

## 🔍 NEW LOW (2026-05-05-d) — Improve per-batch celebrity-homograph detection

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-05-d during D3 RESUME COMPLETED 86-batch run.

**The pattern:** consolidation #4 (after batch 40) archived 31 celebrity+bursa homograph keywords in one bulk pass. Consolidation #8 (after batch 80) archived 117 in one pass. All were keywords like "[celebrity name] bursa" referring to the Turkish city of Bursa, not the anatomical bursa.

**Two interpretations:**
1. Per-batch model is too lenient with celebrity-bursa pairings when seen in isolation; the consolidation model with whole-canvas view recognizes the pattern and bulk-archives.
2. Volume-sorted queue puts these keywords late, so they entered the canvas late and got archived by consolidation rather than per-batch.

**Either way, it's working** — consolidation does what consolidation is supposed to do. But 117 archives in one consolidation pass is expensive (cost $0.699, ~3 min) and slow vs. catching them per-batch.

**Recommended fix:** add a "celebrity-name homograph" few-shot example to the per-batch V4 prompt (`docs/AUTO_ANALYZE_PROMPT_V4.md`). Example pattern: "Queries combining a well-known person's name with a homograph term (e.g., 'X bursa' where bursa could refer to the Turkish city) — archive unless the query has additional context indicating the medical condition." Test on a small Bursitis Test 2 follow-up run.

**Effort:** ~15-30 LOC prompt edit + small validation run. Low priority — current behavior produces correct results.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-05-D STATE block "🚨 New findings surfaced this session" #4; D3 RESUME COMPLETED activity log (consolidations #4 + #8).

**(P-1) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-10-f at code level on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` (W#2 polish session #11; commit `d715cde`). vklf.com auth: silent token refresh + retry on 401.** Pre-fix: when a vklf.com user came back to the site after >1 hour (the Supabase access-token TTL), the page surfaced a 401 'Invalid or expired token' error directly (e.g., `Could not load Projects (401): {"error":"Invalid or expired token"}`); user had to manually sign out + sign back in to recover. **Fix shipped 2026-05-10-f:** `src/lib/authFetch.ts` refactored to a tested factory shape — new `makeAuthFetch({supabase, fetchFn})` factory accepts deps for unit-test substitution; production export `authFetch` is bound against a lazily-initialised Supabase singleton + global `fetch`. Lazy init required because the Node test runner imports `authFetch.ts` without `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL` set in env, and an eager `createClient()` at module scope crashed the test process. Wrapper behavior: (1) read cached session, throw "Not authenticated — no active session" if no session at all (existing behavior preserved); (2) build `Authorization: Bearer <token>` header + first fetch attempt; (3) NEW — if status === 401, call `supabase.auth.refreshSession()`; (4) NEW — if refresh succeeds AND a new `access_token` exists, rebuild headers with the new token + re-fire the fetch ONCE; return the retry's response (no further retries — second 401 is final); (5) NEW — if refresh fails (`error` or no new token), return the original 401 unchanged. Non-401 statuses (200/404/500/etc.) and the no-session-at-all path are unchanged. **Failure-path forced-picker per Rule 14f:** director picked Option (a) — return original 401 to caller as-is when refresh ALSO fails, so existing error handlers at the 76 call sites behave exactly like today; minimal change, zero caller-code edits, no global navigation side-effect from a low-level fetch wrapper. **Rule 15 autonomous pick noted in commit:** refresh-failure caused by network-offline gets the same treatment as refresh-failure caused by expired refresh token — both return the original 401. **Test coverage shipped (`src/lib/authFetch.test.ts` NEW):** 7 tests via `node:test` + `node:assert/strict` covering 200 happy path, 401-refresh-success-retry-200, 401-refresh-success-retry-401-no-loop, 401-refresh-fails-returns-original, 500-no-refresh, no-session-throws, POST-body-and-caller-headers-preserved-across-retry. **Verification:** **400/400 src/lib tests pass** (was 393; +7 authFetch tests); `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; `npm run build` clean (51 routes, no change); `npx eslint src/lib/authFetch.ts src/lib/authFetch.test.ts` clean; project-wide `npx eslint src` 13 errors / 39 warnings — exact baseline parity (zero new errors/warnings introduced). **Push status:** push to `origin/workflow-2-competition-scraping` does NOT redeploy vklf.com (only push-to-main does). Deploy + browser-verify of the 1-hour-token-expiry scenario rolls into the next W#2 → main deploy session along with the deferred P3B verification of P-3 broader scope. **Cross-references:** `src/lib/authFetch.ts` (the factory + production export); `src/lib/authFetch.test.ts` (7 tests); `CORRECTIONS_LOG.md` 2026-05-08-b informational entry (Finding 2) on deploy-session verification-scope gap (the slip that produced the original P-1 capture); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Waypoint #1 attempt #2 row (where the 401 surfaced) + the new "Polish session #11" section appended this session for the next deploy-session browser-verify.

Code-side polish gap identified by reading `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/api-client.ts:48-62`: `authedFetch()` doesn't catch `fetch()`'s native `TypeError: Failed to fetch` that occurs in offline scenarios. **(P-4) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-08-d (code-level) + ✅ BROWSER-VERIFIED 2026-05-09 attempt #5 Amazon sponsored-ads SSPA-redirect detection (NEW 2026-05-08-c).** Director observed during Waypoint #1 attempt #3 Step S3-7 walkthrough: *"The + icon shows for organic search results but not the sponsored ads (which should also show the + icon)."* Root cause: Amazon's sponsored ads route through `/sspa/click?ie=UTF8&spc=...&url=%2Fdp%2F{ASIN}...` patterns where the actual `/dp/{ASIN}` lives URL-encoded inside the `url=` query parameter; `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/platform-modules/amazon.ts:matchesProduct` ASIN_RE only matches literal path-level `/dp/` or `/gp/product/`, so sponsored-ad links get NO `+ Add` button. **Fix shipped 2026-05-08-d:** new `decodeSspaInner(href)` reads `pathname === '/sspa/click'` cases, pulls `searchParams.get('url')` (auto-decoded once), prepends `${protocol}//${host}`, and feeds the result back through ASIN_RE. **(P-5) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-08-d (code-level) + ✅ BROWSER-VERIFIED 2026-05-09 attempt #5 Live-page Highlight Terms application (NEW 2026-05-08-c — director directive).** Director surfaced expectation during Waypoint #1 attempt #3 Step S3-7 walkthrough: *"Secondly, the highlight words are not being highlighted on the amazon results page."* Then clarified scope: *"When using the competition scraping extension, the highlight words should be highlighted on the page that the user is on."* Pre-fix state: zero live-page highlight code in `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/`; popup UI persisted Highlight Terms per-Project to `chrome.storage.local` but no content-script reading. **Fix shipped 2026-05-08-d (Rule 18 design Read-It-Back done before coding; director approved design before coding started):** new file `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/highlight-terms.ts` (~240 LOC) + `.test.ts` (~120 LOC unit tests on regex + colormap pure logic). Reads `highlightTerms:<projectId>` from `chrome.storage.local` via existing `getHighlightTerms()`. Match algorithm: case-insensitive + word-boundary anchored (\b — `cat` does NOT match `category`) + multi-word phrase support with literal spaces broadened to \s+ (matches non-breaking-space + line-break variations) + longest-first ordering on the alternation so multi-word terms beat their substrings. DOM walking: TreeWalker over text nodes only, skipping subtrees rooted at script/style/noscript/textarea/input/iframe/svg/math/code/pre + contenteditable elements + our own `.plos-cs-*` UI (so highlights never appear inside the URL-add form or floating + button). Wraps matches with `<mark class="plos-cs-highlight">` styled inline per-term using existing `getContrastTextColor()` for foreground auto-flip (light backgrounds → black text; dark → white). Live updates: `chrome.storage.onChanged` listener fires when popup edits terms (popup-side ↔ live-page sync without page refresh); MutationObserver hookup via existing orchestrator observer (shares one observer; debounced 250ms; runs on SPA navigation + infinite-scroll new tiles); SPA navigation refresh via existing `popstate` hook. Performance safeguards: 50-term soft cap with `console.warn` + truncate; 500KB body-text cap with skip + warn (Amazon search results typically ~50KB); initial pass via `requestIdleCallback` with `setTimeout(...,0)` fallback. Cleanup wired into orchestrator teardown. Wired into `orchestrator.ts` after `ensureStylesInjected()`; failures don't break the rest of orchestrator (try/catch around init). **NOT done in P-5 (could revisit as future polish):** highlighting inside contenteditable / textarea (typing would corrupt); de-duplicating overlapping multi-term matches (today: adjacent highlights — could compute non-overlapping intervals); per-host opt-out. **Cross-references:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/highlight-terms.ts` + `.test.ts` (code site); `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/orchestrator.ts` (integration site); `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/styles.ts` (`.plos-cs-highlight` CSS); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_DESIGN.md §B` 2026-05-08-c (origin directive) + 2026-05-08-d (fix shipped + design choices); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Waypoint #1 attempt #3 row (origin) + attempt #5 row (browser re-verify when added).

**(P-7) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-08-d (code-level) + ✅ BROWSER-VERIFIED 2026-05-09 attempt #5 URL-add overlay positioning — don't occlude the product listing being saved (NEW 2026-05-08-d — director directive).** Director directive surfaced during Waypoint #1 attempt #4 Step S3-12 walkthrough: *"When the overlay opens to allow the user to add a url, it shouldn't open directly on top of the very product listing for which the url is being added because many times the user may need to look at the product listing to type in the product name, type or brand."* Pre-fix: URL-add overlay opened centered in the viewport via the backdrop's `display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: center` layout, fully occluding whatever was in the viewport center — typically the product card the user just clicked the "+" on. **Fix shipped 2026-05-08-d:** added optional `triggerRect?: DOMRect | null` to `UrlAddFormProps`; threaded through `FloatingAddButton.onClick(href, triggerRect)` callback contract update + `currentLinkRect` storage at button-show time (via `link.getBoundingClientRect()`); new `computeFormPosition()` in `url-add-form.ts` places the form on the side of the viewport opposite the trigger's horizontal center (left half → form right; right half → form left), anchored near top of viewport with 16px margin, clamped for narrow viewports. Falls back to centered layout when `triggerRect === null` (right-click context-menu fallback path — no trigger element to position relative to). **Cross-references:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/url-add-form.ts` (computeFormPosition + form positioning); `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/floating-add-button.ts` (currentLinkRect storage + onClick contract); `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/orchestrator.ts` (handleAddRequest threading); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_DESIGN.md §B` 2026-05-08-d append-only entry per Rule 18 mid-build directive Read-It-Back; `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Waypoint #1 attempt #4 row (where directive surfaced — added end of attempt #5 session).

**(P-8) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-08-d (code-level) + ✅ BROWSER-VERIFIED 2026-05-09 attempt #5 ✓ already-saved icon punches through URL-add overlay — z-index conflict (NEW 2026-05-08-d).** Director observed during Waypoint #1 attempt #4 Step S3-16 walkthrough: *"if a listing that is next to it had its url added previously, its checkmark shows up on top of the new overlay (which it shouldn't)."* Root cause: yesterday's `f4226ca` ✓-icon visibility-boost set `.plos-cs-saved-icon` z-index to `2147483647` (max int32) so the icon would beat Amazon's chrome — but this also equals the `.plos-cs-form` z-index, AND `.plos-cs-saved-icon` has `position: relative` which creates its own stacking context. Two stacking contexts at max-int z-index → DOM-order / sub-context-rendering wins, in this case the saved-icon punches through the open URL-add overlay. **Fix shipped 2026-05-08-d:** layered z-index tiers in `styles.ts` — page-overlay tier `999990` (saved-icon + add-button + dismiss × + overlay-banner) sits above host page chrome; modal-backdrop tier `999998` covers the page-overlay tier when modal opens; modal-content tier `999999` is above its own backdrop. Amazon's chrome max-z-index is ~5000-10000, so 999990 has ~100× headroom. Single-file CSS change, ~5 lines effective. **Browser re-verified 2026-05-09:** with overlay open on a product card next to a saved-✓ product, the dimmed backdrop covers the entire page including the ✓ icon — no punch-through. **Cross-references:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/styles.ts` (z-index tier definitions in CSS + leading comment block documenting the tier system); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_DESIGN.md §B` 2026-05-08-d append-only entry per Rule 18; `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Waypoint #1 attempt #4 + #5 rows.

**(P-9) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-10-b at code level on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` (W#2 polish session #8) + ✅ DEPLOYED 2026-05-10-c to `main` + ✅ BROWSER-VERIFIED 2026-05-10-c on vklf.com — ALL 9 STEPS PASSED across 4 platforms (Ebay search/detail + Walmart search + chrome://extensions Errors panel zero-new-cap-warning entries + soft 50-term-count warning still fires + Amazon/Etsy spot-checks no regression + Walmart live-edit updates within ~1-2s). Highlight-terms 500KB body-text cap too aggressive — blocks Highlight Terms on Ebay + Walmart pages; fires repeatedly on Walmart heavy-SPA pages (NEW 2026-05-09 attempt #5; data point added 2026-05-09-b: Walmart search confirmed at 656,627 bytes via chrome://extensions Errors panel: `[PLOS] page text length (656627) exceeds highlight cap (500000); skipping highlight pass.` on `https://www.walmart.com/search?q=bursitis` — director re-confirmed P-9 status during P-6 session #6 wrap-up; SHIPPED 2026-05-10-b — chunked/incremental highlight pass via `requestIdleCallback` + cap REMOVED entirely. New exported `processInChunks<T>(items, processItem, options)` generic helper (default chunk size 500 nodes ≈ 10-15ms/chunk; pluggable `yieldFn` for testing; honors `CancellationSignal` between chunks). `applyHighlightsTo` is now async + chunked. `startLiveHighlighting.refresh()` rewritten for last-wins cancellation — each new refresh cancels in-flight pass before starting; latest DOM/term state always becomes eventual visible state. Removing the cap auto-resolved the backlog's recommended (e) dedupe warning + (f) skip-if-unchanged measurement — no cap → no warning → no `document.body.textContent.length` re-measure overhead. 9 new tests added to `highlight-terms.test.ts` for `processInChunks`).** Surfaced during Waypoint #1 attempt #5 Ebay (S3-26) + Walmart (S3-28) walkthroughs. P-5 (live-page Highlight Terms shipped 2026-05-08-d) included a 500KB body-text safeguard that skips the highlight pass on pages exceeding the cap, intended to avoid main-thread freeze on very large pages. Three related symptoms with the same root cause: (1) Highlight Terms don't appear on **Ebay search results** because page text exceeds cap (~1.5MB body text); (2) Highlight Terms don't appear on **Ebay listing detail pages** either (~1.58MB body text — confirmed via Console diagnostic 2026-05-09); (3) Highlight Terms don't appear on **Walmart search results** (~636-675KB) AND the cap fires **~20+ times per Walmart page-load** because Walmart's heavy React re-renders + dynamic ad loading trigger the orchestrator's MutationObserver re-scan repeatedly even with the 250ms debounce — each re-scan re-runs the highlight pass which re-runs the cap check + re-measures `document.body.innerText` (an expensive operation). chrome://extensions Errors panel accumulates one entry per cap-fire on Ebay; ~20+ per Walmart page-load. **Amazon search results stay below cap (~50KB) so the issue doesn't surface there.** Etsy pages stay below cap so highlights work cleanly on Etsy. **Fix options:** (a) bump the cap to ~5MB (covers Ebay's typical sizes; risky for very-large pages); (b) make cap user-configurable per-platform (good default + escape hatch); (c) **switch to chunked/incremental highlight pass via requestIdleCallback** that handles arbitrary-size pages without main-thread freeze (best UX; biggest engineering — likely best long-term answer); (d) lower the log severity from `console.warn` → `console.debug` (Chrome's Errors panel only catches warn+ severity); (e) only emit the warning ONCE per page-load (deduplicate via a per-page-load Set or flag); (f) tighten the MutationObserver debounce on heavy-SPA platforms OR skip the cap re-check if page text length hasn't changed significantly since last check (avoid the perf cost of re-measuring body text on every re-scan). **Recommended combination:** (c) for the underlying perf concern + (e) + (f) for the noise + perf. Estimated ~90-120 min for (c) standalone or ~30-50 min for (e)+(f) interim fix. **Cross-references:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/highlight-terms.ts` (the 500KB cap site + console.warn site); `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/orchestrator.ts` (MutationObserver debounce site); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Waypoint #1 attempt #5 row (origin).

**(P-10) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-05-10-b at code level on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` (W#2 polish session #8) + ✅ DEPLOYED 2026-05-10-c to `main` + ✅ BROWSER-VERIFIED 2026-05-10-c on vklf.com — ALL 10 STEPS PASSED (direct paste of saved Walmart URL → banner within ~1s + auto-dismiss; SPA navigation to saved Walmart product reliably 5/5 times across different products; unsaved-product correctly suppresses banner; unsaved → saved navigation re-fires banner; refresh re-fires; manual × dismiss correctly suppresses re-fire; Amazon + Ebay + Etsy spot-checks no regression). AlreadySavedOverlay banner intermittent on saved-URL navigation, observed on Walmart heavy-SPA pages (NEW 2026-05-09 attempt #5; SHIPPED 2026-05-10-b — three orchestrator changes: (1) `maybeShowDetailOverlay()` dedupes by `location.href` via new `lastOverlayUrl` closure variable (set BEFORE recognition match so navigate-away-and-back correctly re-fires); (2) new `scheduleDetailOverlayCheck()` 150ms-debounced cancellable timer ensures only the final URL gets a banner check after pushState bursts; (3) MutationObserver-based SPA URL change detection via new `lastObservedUrl` closure variable — checks `location.href !== lastObservedUrl` inside the existing 250ms-debounced rescan callback and triggers the overlay-check debouncer if changed. **Critical technical wrinkle that drove the design:** Chrome content scripts run in an **isolated world** with their own `window.history`, so patching `pushState` in content-script context does NOT intercept host-page React Router calls (Walmart, etc.). Backlog's suggested fix #2 (intercept `history.pushState`/`replaceState`) doesn't work cross-context; the MutationObserver is the cross-context-safe signal since SPA navigation always causes immediate DOM mutation. Initial-load detail-overlay check at orchestrator startup also routes through the debouncer — gives Walmart's React time to settle URL after content-script load. Cleanup function clears any pending overlay-check + rescan timers on teardown. Per existing extension test convention (DOM-touching code verified end-to-end in browser, only pure logic unit-tested), no new unit tests added for these orchestrator changes — relies on next waypoint walkthrough for browser verification across Amazon + Ebay + Etsy + Walmart).** Director observation during Waypoint #1 attempt #5 S3-28 Walmart walkthrough: *"the green overlay that is supposed to tell me that the url is already added doesn't show sometimes."* The AlreadySavedOverlay banner (✓ This URL is already in your project · <Project Name>) appears RELIABLY on Amazon + Ebay + Etsy detail pages but INTERMITTENTLY on Walmart detail pages. Likely root causes worth investigating in the fix: (a) **storage-hydration race** — content script's saved-URL-check fires BEFORE the saved-URL list has loaded from `chrome.storage.local` for that platform; check sees empty list → no match → no banner; (b) **Walmart SPA navigation** — Walmart's React routing uses `history.pushState()` directly to navigate between pages; the orchestrator listens for the `popstate` event, which fires on back/forward but NOT on programmatic `pushState`; SPA navigations between Walmart pages don't trigger the URL-change check; (c) **initial-page-load timing** — the canonical URL extraction may not be stable at the moment the banner-check fires (e.g., URL changes from `/search?q=...` to `/ip/{id}` as page loads). **Fix sketch:** (1) wrap the saved-URL-check in a small wait-for-storage-hydration delay or use `chrome.storage.onChanged` to fire the check whenever storage updates; (2) intercept `history.pushState` + `history.replaceState` (monkey-patch on `window` or use a polyfill like 'history-events') in addition to `popstate` so SPA navigations are caught; (3) re-fire the banner-check on `document.readyState` transitions ('interactive' → 'complete'). Estimated ~30-50 LOC + careful regression testing across Amazon + Ebay + Etsy + Walmart to confirm no regressions on platforms that already work. **Cross-references:** `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/already-saved-overlay.ts` (the overlay component); `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/orchestrator.ts` (popstate listener + URL-change detection); `COMPETITION_SCRAPING_VERIFICATION_BACKLOG.md` Waypoint #1 attempt #5 row (origin).

## 🔍 NEW MEDIUM (2026-05-04-c) — `[FLAKE]` telemetry visibility puzzle

**Status:** DISCOVERED 2026-05-04-c during D3 retry batch 1's pool-exhaustion event; investigation deferred to a small standalone session.

**The puzzle:** the flake-counter telemetry shipped 2026-05-04 (`src/lib/flake-counter.ts` + 38 `recordFlake` call sites across 19 DB-backed routes) should have logged a `[FLAKE]` line for every catch-block error. During the 2026-05-04-c D3 batch 1 pool-exhaustion event, ~28 errors fired within ~0.1 sec. Director's Vercel runtime logs paste showed all ~28 with full stack traces but **NO line beginning with `[FLAKE]`** visible. PATCH /keywords/[keywordId] WAS in the wired list per the 2026-05-04 STATE block (+2 recordFlake calls per the manifest).

**Three possibilities:**

1. **Vercel UI display issue.** The runtime logs view may show only the first console.error per request (the existing `console.error('<X> error:', error)`); the second console.error from `recordFlake` (called BEFORE the existing one) may be hidden in a collapsed per-request view. Director's paste might have been from a high-level summary view that shows one line per request. Test next session: click into a single failed request to expand its full log; look for `[FLAKE]` line.

2. **Flake-counter not firing on these endpoints.** Would be a real wiring bug. The 2026-05-04 work was supposed to be exact 1-to-1 across all 38 catch blocks. Re-verify the deploy actually shipped the wiring (deployed bundle inspection on Vercel; OR `git diff` between 2026-05-04 commit and current main).

3. **Format issue.** `recordFlake` calls `console.error` which Vercel routes to runtime logs; possible but unlikely given the helper's unit tests cover this.

**Investigation plan (next session, standalone):**
- (i) Read Vercel logs at the next live error event using expanded per-request view; look for `[FLAKE]` lines.
- (ii) If absent in expanded view: re-confirm `recordFlake` calls present in deployed bundle (check Vercel deploy artifacts OR confirm via `git log --oneline src/lib/flake-counter.ts src/app/api/`).
- (iii) If present in bundle but not in logs: write a small targeted test that triggers a PATCH error (e.g., posting an invalid keyword update) and confirm the `[FLAKE]` line appears in dev-server output.

**Why MEDIUM, not HIGH:** the underlying functionality (errors propagate to user; existing console.error captures full stack trace) is unaffected. The visibility gap only affects our ability to grade the rate-fix's effectiveness empirically — important but not user-facing.

**Cross-references:** `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` POST-2026-05-04-C STATE block "Open question" section; `PLATFORM_ARCHITECTURE.md §10` "📊 Platform-wide flake-rate telemetry" entry (the original 2026-05-04 work).

## 🔔 SCALE SESSION 0 — OUTCOME C FIRED 2026-04-28 (build path activated)

The empirical validation pre-step of `INPUT_CONTEXT_SCALING_DESIGN.md` (Scale Session 0) ran 2026-04-28. Director ran a full-Bursitis V3 Auto-Analyze on Sonnet 4.6 (151 of 281 batches completed before stopping) plus a separate Opus 4.7 cost test at run start.

**Empirical findings:**

1. **Sonnet 4.6 hit the 200k context wall at batch 151** — input grew from 19,929 tokens (empty canvas) → 220,091 tokens (canvas of ~700 topics). The wall was reached well before the run could complete; an additional ~130 batches would have been needed.
2. **Opus 4.7 was economically prohibitive** — director's cost test at run start showed per-batch costs approached or exceeded $1, vs. ~$0.30–$0.85 on Sonnet 4.6. Director switched back to Sonnet 4.6.
3. **Per-batch cost on Sonnet 4.6 grew monotonically** with canvas size (~$0.20 → ~$0.85), driven entirely by input-token growth (the prompt body itself stays cached at ~18k tokens). Total run cost: ~$70–80 for 54% completion.

**Trigger conditions met (per `INPUT_CONTEXT_SCALING_DESIGN.md §0`):**
- Outcome C: V3 + Opus 4.7 still hits wall or has unacceptable cost — **YES, fired**.
- Threshold (b): a production project's canvas exceeded ~600 topics under standard 200k window — **YES, the Bursitis run reached ~700 topics**.

**Effect on roadmap:**
- **Scale Session B is now the next-priority forward action** for Workflow #1 build work (per `INPUT_CONTEXT_SCALING_DESIGN.md §6` locked plan): schema migration adding `intentFingerprint` column + applier extension + AI-generated backfill script.
- Scale Sessions C, D, E follow B in sequence per the locked plan.

**Three additional findings from the same run that are NOT scaling-related (separate sections below):**
- 🚨 **HIGH-severity canvas-blanking bug** (batches 70 + 134) — wiring layer intermittently sent ~20k tokens of input (no canvas state) instead of full canvas; model rebuilt from scratch; reconciliation flipped 84 keywords/event to Reshuffled status; 168 keywords across the two events stuck in Reshuffled forever because batch queue is fixed at run-start. NOT polish — see "Canvas-blanking bug" section below.
- 4 new Phase-1 polish items (Mid-run batch queue refresh + Skeleton View on canvas + AST split-view row alignment + Topics table row numbers) — see "NEW Phase-1 polish item" entries below.
- 2 new architectural design items (action-by-action feedback + second-pass refinement workflow; intelligent hybrid cost/quality strategy) — see new sections below.

- **Phase D (documentation overhaul):** 11-document handoff system with Document Lifecycle Management (DLMS)

- **Phase M Checkpoint 5 (2026-04-17):** All server-side API routes aligned with new schema; `npm run build` clean; committed at `14d68e7`
- **Phase M Checkpoint 6 (2026-04-17, chat `7a745b12-...`):** Built `/projects` page and `/projects/[projectId]` detail page. ## 🎯 Post-Phase-M — Claude Code Migration (TOP PRIORITY) — user executes, no Claude chat needed

After Phase M is fully deployed and verified (DONE as of 2026-04-17), the user performs a ~30-minute offline migration:

1. **Install Claude Code** in Codespaces (`npm install -g @anthropic-ai/claude-code` or current equivalent — check https://docs.claude.com for current install command)
2. **Authenticate** (uses existing Anthropic account)
3. **Smoke test** — run `claude` in Codespaces terminal, ask a trivial question, verify file reading works
4. **Read `docs/CLAUDE_CODE_MIGRATION.md`** end-to-end — this is the user's orientation to the new methodology
5. **Ready for first Claude Code session** (Phase 1g-test kickoff)

This migration is logged as a roadmap item (this section) and captured in `docs/CLAUDE_CODE_MIGRATION.md`. No code changes. No Claude chat required during the migration itself.

Walks the entire AST table; flips on-canvas-Unsorted/Reshuffled to AI-Sorted (heals Bug 1 silent placements + reabsorbs reshuffled keywords just re-placed); flips off-canvas-AI-Sorted to NEW `'Reshuffled'` status (Bug 2 reshuffle ghosts surfaced as visible alarm per director's Option B framing during drift-check). Each off-canvas flip emits a structured `aaLog` line forward-compatible with future `ai_feedback_records` schema. New Reshuffled status: yellow `.ast-pill-r` badge in AST + RemovedKeyword display + TIFTable; column is `String @default("Unsorted")` so no schema migration; type union in `useKeywords.ts` extended; ASTTable + MTTable + TIFTable filter logic treats Reshuffled as Unsorted-equivalent; AutoAnalyze "Unsorted only" scope renamed to "Unsorted + Reshuffled" with both values picked up by default. **Item #2 — Salvage-ignored-keywords mechanism** as new `runSalvage()` in AutoAnalyze. Trigger: `runLoop` validation flow detects HC3-only failure (every error starts "Missing " — no HC4/HC5 lost-data triggers) and fires salvage instead of full retry per director's Option A framing. Builds Change-6-template follow-up prompt at runtime with Q5-resolution wording (auto-archive language); calls `callApi`; salvage cost added to `batch.cost`; parses three blocks (DELTA ROWS, IRRELEVANT_KEYWORDS, REEVALUATION REPORT). Delta rows merged into `originalResult.topicsTableTsv` via refactored `mergeDelta(deltaTsv, baseTsv?)` (the optional second arg is new). IRRELEVANT_KEYWORDS POSTed PER-keyword to `/api/projects/[projectId]/removed-keywords` with `removedSource='auto-ai-detected-irrelevant'` + model's reason as `aiReasoning`. Archived ids removed from `batch.keywordIds`/`batch.keywords` + `onRefreshKeywords()` synced; re-validation; doApply if pass; falls through to retry on salvage error or unresolved missing. **Item #4 — P3-F8 four-function canvas-layout port** as new `src/lib/canvas-layout.ts` (321 lines) with all four functions as pure exports that mutate passed nodes in place. `calcNodeHeight(node)` uses browser canvas measureText with word-aware wrap matching HTML's `cvsWrap`; respects `userMinH`; SSR-safe fallback. `runLayoutPass(nodes, pathways, collapsed?)` is the 4-step holistic pass (reset roots → tree-walk type-aware placement → 60-pass overlap resolution → pathway separation). `autoLayoutChild(child, parent, relType, allNodes, collapsed?)` is type-aware (linear = align parent-left below all peer subtrees; nested = align parent-center+indent below nested siblings only); moves entire child subtree by delta. `separatePathways(nodes, pathways, collapsed?)` is horizontal pathway push-apart. Constants mirror HTML except NODE_W=220 + NESTED_INDENT=30 (kept React's existing values). Wired into `AutoAnalyze.doApply` step 7.5 — fires on every batch's apply per Q1 lockdown — and into `CanvasPanel.handleLinkClick` for type-aware auto-position on parent-child link form (coalesced single-server-PATCH for parent-link change + position changes). Build clean. Single commit `6c09e50` — **NOT YET PUSHED, awaiting director approval per Rule 9 deploy gate.** **Two NEW Phase-1 polish ROADMAP items captured during drift-check** (see below): "P3-F7 root-cause audit" (HC5 text-matching audit + canvas rebuild text-match audit + new HC6 "no keyword unlinks" check + Bursitis 49-ghost spot-audit) + "Keyword accounting + ghost detection panel" (history-of-every-keyword-ever-added compared against AST ∪ RemovedTerms; admin Ghost Keywords panel with Restore/Archive bulk actions). Both schedule with Session 4 or 5; not blocking.
